# Codex logic gate — is the relevance-driven corpus math LOGICALLY SOUND + loophole closed?

ADVERSARIAL §-1.1 auditor. The operator caught a fatal loophole in a prior cost model: the pipeline discovers
~1,000 sources but truncates to a fixed top-K (evidence_rows[:PG_LIVE_MAX_EV_TO_GEN]) — dropping high-value sources
by POSITION, not quality. A workflow produced the redesign below (full doc: outputs/I-meta-002/corpus_relevance_
driven_logic.md — READ IT). Sub-agents may have leaked the forbidden advisor tool — re-verify yourself. Rule whether
the redesign is LOGICALLY SOUND and the loophole is genuinely closed, and whether the numbers hold. YAML verdict FIRST. iter 1.


## The redesign to rule on (full arithmetic in the doc)
LOOPHOLE: 234 sub-queries x ~12 hits -> ~1,000 candidates, cut at FETCH_CAP=40 (run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1627) then
MAX_EV_TO_GEN=20 (:2266) = ~96% dropped by POSITION, silently (drops go to a best-effort Path-B trace, not a manifest
count). CONFIRMED by me via grep: the [:max_ev] slice + caps exist.
SOUND MODEL: keep every source clearing 3 bars — tier (T1-T4 admissible), relevance (_row_relevance >= adaptive tau,
evidence_selector.py:377), dedup-by-finding (collapse same-finding sources to 1 finding w/ N provenance ptrs). N =
survivors, NO fixed max. MAP-REDUCE: per-source digest call (MAP, parallel, ~2.5k in/0.5k out, never hits context
wall) -> hierarchical synthesis over ~500-tok digests (REDUCE) -> full-span re-read ONLY for cited claims.
HONEST SPLIT: of ~1,000, ~120-200 genuinely relevant kept, ~800 true noise dropped (off-topic/news/marketing/stub/
dup-finding). CLAIM: keeping ALL 1,000 would HURT quality (DeepTRACE / lost-in-the-middle — covering set, not biggest
set). The OLD cap dropped the WRONG ~960 (kept top-40 incl noise, killed relevant past rank 40).
COST f(N) [EU-sovereign 9xH100+1xA100 @ $33.86/hr; claims(N)=24.7*N^0.489 fit through measured (20,107) +
Codex-corrected (200,330); wall=0.9+0.0145*N hr]:
  N=200 -> 330 claims, 3.8hr, $129 EU
  N=500 -> 517 claims, 8.2hr, $277 EU
  N=1000 -> 725 claims, 15.4hr, $523 EU
  N=1500(all-relevant) -> 884 claims, 22.6hr, $770 EU
Generator tokens trivial (<$2.30 even at N=1500); driver = 4-role verifier GPU wall-clock.
CLOSURE BUILD: kill both count-caps -> relevance/tier floors + corpus_funnel manifest block (discovered/dropped-by-
reason/kept/tau); build per-source evidence_reducer (MAP); cluster into findings; re-point synthesis at findings;
WIRE the 4-role verifiers (CLAIM: Mirror/Sentinel/Judge are NOT in the sweep path today, grep=0 — only entailment_judge
+ one external_evaluation run); saturation stop-rule (stop when new-unique-finding rate < ~1/20 for 2 rounds).

## The real risks to rule on
1. Is claims(N)=24.7*N^0.489 a defensible model or an OVERFIT on 2 points? Sanity-check N=1000->725, N=1500->884.
2. Is wall=0.9+0.0145*N honest, or does it under/over-state the 4-role GPU time at high N?
3. Is the relevance-density (~120-200 of 1,000) defensible, or could the real relevant set be much larger (making
   the dump worse) — and does the model still hold if so? (The doc says it slides up the same f(N) curve.)
4. Verify grep: are Mirror/Sentinel/Judge genuinely ABSENT from run_honest_sweep_r3.py's path? (Load-bearing — it
   means the locked 4-role gate is not actually exercised by the shipping run.)
5. Is "keeping all 1,000 hurts" (DeepTRACE/lost-in-the-middle) FAIR, or a convenient excuse to cap? Cite if real.
6. Does the relevance-threshold + map-reduce design ACTUALLY remove all silent position-based truncation, or is
   there a residual hidden cap (context budget per section, dedup over-collapse, fetch concurrency)?

.\docs\process\polaris_task_cycle_proposal_2026_05_28.md:324:5. **Live 4-role smoke (Gate B) is frozen by design.** `pathB_run_gate._assert_architecture_coverage()` raises while `lock status == codex_approved_pending_operator_signature`. .\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:9:POLARIS is one clinical-grade deep-research machine. A research question goes in, and a signed report comes out where every single claim has been checked against the exact source text. Inside, four AI models work in a line: a Generator writes the answer, a Mirror checks each claim is really supported, a Sentinel hunts for made-up statements, and a Judge gives every claim one of five honest grades. Around that line we wrap two more things: the power to pause and resume at any stage without paying twice, and a memory that snowballs, so the machine remembers what it already proved and can catch a new claim that contradicts something we verified weeks ago. The one rule above all others: we do a full dry run and confirm the whole machine is correct before we spend a single dollar on rented GPUs. Correct means a deep, line-by-line review of every output, every reasoning step, and every log, done independently by both Claude and Codex.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:25:With that flag in hand, the claim goes to the Mirror, which is Cohere Command A Plus. The Mirror runs in two passes. One pass gives a grounded answer with citations. A separate pass, not in grounding mode, returns a clean calibration verdict. Two passes are needed because the citation mode and the structured-verdict mode cannot be combined on this model. Then the claim goes to the Sentinel, which is IBM Granite Guardian. The Sentinel answers a yes-or-no question about whether the claim is grounded. There is a lethal detail here: for this model, yes means ungrounded, a hallucination was detected, and no means grounded. Getting that polarity backwards would let fabrications walk straight through, so it is tested explicitly. Finally the claim reaches the Judge, which is Qwen. The Judge is the terminal decision-maker. It takes the Mirror's calibration, the Sentinel's flag, and the memory's cross-time flag, and it issues exactly one of five verdicts: verified, partial, unsupported, fabricated, or unreachable. The Judge is forced to pick one of those five and cannot wander off. After each claim, we append one line to a verdict ledger and bump a cursor. That is a checkpoint too.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:27:When the Judge is done, one verdict drives three things at once, and this is the payoff of building it as one machine instead of three stapled-together parts. First, report release. A fabricated claim gets refused in place immediately and gates the run, because a fabrication happening at all is a red flag regardless of cleanup. An unsupported claim gets one rewrite-and-recheck, and if it still fails it is refused in place and the run is gated only if what remains is too thin. We never count or rate fabrications; a single one in a material claim is enough. Even a gated run still emits a report as a reviewable verdict artifact, never silence. Second, memory write eligibility. Verified and partial claims are eligible to be remembered; fabricated and unreachable claims never enter the memory. Third, the claim is queued for the final audit.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:29:Then the single memory write happens. For each verified claim, the machine builds the identity key. A brand-new claim becomes a new node. A claim that matches an existing one with agreeing numbers is a re-confirmation; we do not duplicate it, we increment its confirmation count and link the runs. Crucially, the claim is written at the lower trust tier, called provisional, because the Judge alone is still just an automated check. If the memory store is unavailable, the write fails loudly. It does not quietly return nothing, which is the exact silent-degradation bug that left today's store empty.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:35:Where does the memory plug in? It is a cross-cutting layer wrapped around the locked four models, never a new model inside the line. It reads twice and writes once: it reads trusted priors at Generator time, it reads for cross-time contradictions just before the Judge, and it writes after the Judge. Both reads are signals only. The Judge always decides. The lock that pins the four models pins models and roles, not the words we feed into a prompt, so handing the Generator a memory-derived evidence row is provably not a change to the locked architecture. In the lock file, the memory and the pause layer are declared under a brand-new top-level key that sits beside the four required roles, not inside them, so the freeze gate that counts the four roles never even sees it.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:41:First, the honest truth about what zero-spend can and cannot mean. A literal full dry run of the whole machine for zero dollars on rented GPUs is impossible. Two of the four models, the Mirror and the Sentinel, are not available the way the Generator is; to get real output from them we must rent a GPU. So you cannot produce a real Mirror answer or a real Sentinel answer to audit without spending at least a little. We honor the rule, not by pretending a free full run exists, but by making the first spend a single, small, bounded run that is itself the dry run, fully audited by both Claude and Codex before any sustained spend follows.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:45:Here is what Gate A runs, all for zero GPU dollars. The whole orchestration runs for real. The only thing faked is the network call to each model. We do this through one clean seam: an injectable per-role client. In the real product, that client talks to the real model endpoints. In the dry run, that same client replays recorded responses from fixture files, keyed to each claim. The dispatch code never knows it is being mocked; the mock is injected from outside. This is the single hard build rule, because if the fake lived any higher up, say faking "run the whole Mirror pass," the dry run would prove nothing about how the machine dispatches and flows. The fake must sit at the model-call boundary and nowhere higher.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:47:Around those faked model calls, everything else is real and exercised end to end. The role dispatch and ordering are real. The per-claim Mirror-then-Sentinel-then-Judge flow is real. The deterministic Python sentence check is real. The release routing is real. The memory write of verified claims is real, on fixtures. The pause and resume is real, on fixtures. Retrieval runs as a couple of single cheap real probes, not a full sweep. And the Generator runs for real and cheap, because it is the one model with a live endpoint. No full-power sweep fires in the dry run; that is strictly after the money gate.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:49:Now, what does green Gate A actually mean. It means every one of these checks passed. The unit and fixture test suites all pass. The lock-consistency checker exits clean, confirming the model slugs and roles in code match the lock. The offline preflight returns clean. The role-dispatch returns exactly four pins, generator, mirror, sentinel, and judge, where today it returns only two. The coverage gate accepts all four pins, tested against a fixture copy of the lock flipped to the locked state, because the real lock is not signed yet. The Sentinel polarity test confirms yes maps to ungrounded and no maps to grounded; an inverted mapping fails the gate. The Judge parser confirms it returns exactly one of the five verdicts. The Mirror two-pass parses, with the citation pass and the separate verdict pass both working. The release routing is correct: a fabricated claim gates the run on occurrence, an unsupported claim gets one rewrite then gates only on thin residual coverage. The completeness check confirms all four roles actually appear in the captured calls. The pause-and-resume integrity holds under crash injection: we kill the run at every checkpoint boundary and confirm the Generator never re-bills, verdicts replay from the cursor, nothing double-writes, and a drifted protocol fingerprint fails the resume closed. The memory write discipline holds: only verified and partial claims enter, fabricated and unreachable never do, the write is idempotent so re-running never double-counts, and the write fails loudly when the store is missing. The cross-time contradiction check fires correctly against a pre-loaded prior. And the three cheap real probes succeed: one search call, one Semantic Scholar call, one tiny Generator generation, each returning real output from a model whose served identity matches the pin.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:51:What does a correct dry run produce for review? It produces one review dossier per question, in two synchronized forms so both auditors can work line by line: a machine-readable trace with one line per claim, and the same rows rendered as readable markdown. Each claim row carries the Generator sentence, its provenance tag, the Mirror's two passes, the Sentinel score and what its polarity means, the deterministic Python result, the Judge's five-way verdict and its reasoning trace, the release action and whether release was allowed, the memory decision and the reason, and one more field that matters for honesty: whether each fixture was a recorded real response or hand-built from the model's contract. Alongside that go the ordered log lines and the two audit ledgers, one from Claude and one from Codex, written into the existing ledger artifact, not a parallel one. Because the models are mocked and free, the dossier can include things too expensive to run live, like killing the run at every single checkpoint and like adversarial memory fixtures that try to poison the graph. That is why Gate A is genuinely strong, not a consolation prize.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:53:And here is the honest boundary, the line the operator must hear travel with any green verdict. Gate A proves the machine is correctly wired and that its control flow and contracts are right. It does not prove the models are good. A canned Sentinel "yes" proves the pipeline routes an ungrounded flag to the right place. It does not prove the real Granite Guardian would actually say "yes" when shown a real fabrication. Gate A validates wiring and logic. Only the first real rental, Gate B, validates model behavior. That boundary is not negotiable, and it is the honest answer to "is the machine ready to spend on."
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:61:For each trap, each auditor independently checks the same things. Is every cited span the exact fetched text, not a title or an abstract, and does the citation resolve in the evidence pool. Does each reasoning step actually follow from its cited evidence, with no leap and no qualitative-negation that slips past a number check. Is the Judge's verdict the right one given the Mirror and Sentinel signals, and does it match the trap's known label, with the Sentinel polarity asserted right there in the trace. Did release routing behave exactly as the trap expects, and was every drop a refuse-in-place with a recorded gap, never a silent deletion. Did only the right claims enter memory, at the provisional tier, with fabrications excluded, the write idempotent, and a simulated store failure raising loudly. Did pause and resume survive a mid-loop crash with the protocol and config fingerprints re-verified and failing closed on injected drift, with the two cursors proving no claim lost and none double-counted, and the final report byte-identical to an uninterrupted run. And are all the logs present and consistent across the resume cursor, the verdict ledger, and the run logs.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:67:The target is one machine, but the build is staged, because some parts cannot be built on top of parts that do not exist yet. You cannot build the memory write on placeholder verdicts; the Judge has to be really emitting verdicts first. So the order is dependency-driven, and it slots into the review-and-gate cycle Codex already approved, inserting the missing orchestration and dry-run steps between building the model adapters and the step that spends money.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:69:Step one, fix the lock. This is an operator-signed change. It corrects the Judge model slug, which still has a small typo, records the per-role serving routes, updates the verdict-format wording, and adds the new beside-the-roles key that declares the memory and pause layers without disturbing the four-role freeze gate. Step two, build the contract tests against fixtures, including the lethal Sentinel polarity test, the Judge five-verdict test, and the Mirror two-pass test. Step three, build the release gate, with fabrication gating on occurrence, unsupported gating on residual coverage, and a hard must-cover gate for the highest-severity clinical items that fires regardless of overall coverage. Step four, build the three model adapters behind one client interface, each shipping with a fixture mock, and no live calls. Step five, the first inserted step, build the orchestration: extend dispatch from two roles to four, run each surviving claim through Mirror, Sentinel, and Judge, add the memory write seam at the provisional tier with loud failure, and add the pause-and-resume checkpoints with the two cursors. Step six, the second inserted step and the gate itself, run the no-spend dry run on the planted traps and have both Claude and Codex run the deep line-by-line review.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:73:There is one economic lever sitting just below the architecture, and I will name it rather than silently pick it. The feasibility work recommends serving the Mirror through Cohere's own Canadian managed endpoint at full precision, which would shrink the unavoidable GPU rental down to just the small Sentinel model. The flow is identical either way, so this is a serving choice, not an architecture change. But it changes the dry-run economics, so it is flagged for the operator to decide on the lock-change issue. The binding decision today still routes both Mirror and Sentinel to rented GPUs.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:85:Fifth, the self-host calibration risk. If the Mirror is self-hosted quantized rather than served full-precision, four-bit serving is proven to run but is untested for preserving calibration, and calibration is the Mirror's entire reason to exist. Should calibration be re-validated before we trust a self-hosted Mirror verdict?
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:87:Sixth, two operator-side prerequisites that are not in this build but block the live path. The runtime lock is still pending operator signature, so the live four-role run is frozen today. And the main branch is not actually enforcing the Codex required check, so the auto-merge-on-approval chain is not live. Both need an operator action outside this sequence.
.\docs\process\polaris_master_blueprint_2026_05_28.md:91:Current honest state, in one breath: the Vast balance is zero, so the first rental cannot happen until the operator loads credit; the lock is approved but not yet signed, so the live four-role run is frozen; the Judge slug typo fix is approved and in flight; the branch protection does not yet enforce the Codex gate; only the Generator is wired today, the other three models have no call sites, the cross-run memory is empty, and pause-resume is off. The blueprint above is the unified target, and the no-spend dry run plus dual review is the structural gate that honors the one rule before any of it costs a dollar. .\docs\process\polaris_gap_analysis_2026_05_28.md:20:**Gap one — the four-role pipeline.** The Generator role is fully wired and real: `src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py` reads the Generator model setting and builds a live client. The other three roles — Mirror, Sentinel, and Judge — are declared as settings in one file, `src/polaris_graph/llm/openrouter_client.py`, and referenced nowhere else. No code ever builds a client for them. There is no calibration pass, no hallucination-detector pass, no final-arbiter pass. The architecture lock at `config/architecture/polaris_runtime_lock.yaml` names all four roles correctly, and a freeze guard in `scripts/dr_benchmark/pathB_run_gate.py` deliberately blocks the gated smoke test until the lock is signed — so today neither the old path nor the new path actually runs four roles. The gap is large. The one main thing to do: build a role-dispatch layer that constructs a client for each of Mirror, Sentinel, and Judge and adds their three call sites after generation. Important wrinkle the operator already decided: two of these models — Cohere Command A+ (Mirror) and Granite Guardian (Sentinel) — are not available on OpenRouter, so they must be self-hosted on rented Vast.ai GPUs, while Generator and Judge stay on OpenRouter. That means the dispatch layer needs two serving modes, and the whole four-role base is blocked on one operator action: the Vast.ai account balance is currently zero and needs credit loaded before Mirror and Sentinel can run anywhere. Also note: the Judge model name in the lock still carries a small typo, but that fix is already approved and in flight under issue I-meta-002 — it is not a fresh discovery.
.\docs\process\polaris_gap_analysis_2026_05_28.md:24:**Gap three — the snowball knowledge graph.** This one is the furthest from real. What exists is a per-run picture in the web UI at `web/app/runs/[runId]/graph/page.tsx`, with an "expand snowball" button that walks the connections within a single run only — it is a viewer, not a memory. There is one cross-run store in `src/polaris_graph/memory/cross_vector.py`, but it is a flat list of text embeddings with no nodes, edges, entities, or relations, so it is not a knowledge graph at all — and it is empty, with zero claims accumulated, and it is wired only into a dormant pipeline the production sweep never touches. There is no store that saves verified claims across runs, and no code anywhere that checks a new run's claims against what was verified in past runs — so the cross-time contradiction catch you want simply does not exist. The gap is large. The one main thing to do: this is design-only for now under issue I-meta-003, and it is deliberately blocked until the four-role base passes a real dry run. So the honest move is to leave it as design and build it after the four roles work.
.\docs\process\polaris_gap_analysis_2026_05_28.md:32:The single highest-value next build step is to finish the four-role base: build the role-dispatch layer and add the three missing call sites for Mirror, Sentinel, and Judge — but this is gated on one operator action first, loading Vast.ai credit, because two of the three new models must be self-hosted there and the balance is currently zero.

.\docs\polaris_step_b_full_set_audit_2026_05_27.md:53:The role-discriminator for Generator vs Mirror is: **the generator carries the first-pass synthesis burden across all six domains.** Raw recall + long-context faithfulness matter MORE than calibration here, because the mirror is the calibration counterweight. .\docs\polaris_step_b_full_set_audit_2026_05_27.md:114:## Role: Mirror

.\docs\vast_ai_budget_i_meta_002.md:167:**Key insight (the discriminator is precision + strategy, NOT a "self-host = better quality" premise):** A and B both serve Mirror at **full precision**, so they are **quality-equivalent** for the benchmark. C is the only one that compromises quality (W4A4 on the calibration role). So "highest quality" does **not** force A over B. ---

# RELEVANCE-DRIVEN CORPUS MODEL — the loophole, the sound replacement, proven in numbers

## 1. THE LOOPHOLE (one numeric line)

Today the pipeline DISCOVERS ~1,000 candidate URLs (234 sub-queries × ~12 hits) but DUMPS them at two fixed-COUNT cuts — `PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP=40` (`run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1627`) then `PG_LIVE_MAX_EV_TO_GEN=20` (`:2266`) — so ~96% of discovered sources are discarded by POSITION, not by relevance/quality, and at full scale the dump is SILENT in the run artifact (fetch-cap drops go only to a best-effort Path-B trace, never to a manifest count). [MEASURED: `manifest.json` `evidence_total:24 → evidence_selected:20 dropped_count:4`; the caps did not even bind on this shallow run, which is exactly why the loss was invisible until the operator did the per-query math.]

## 2. THE LOGICALLY SOUND MODEL (relevance threshold + map-reduce)

**Selection rule (replaces both numeric caps):** keep every source that clears ALL three bars, drop the rest with a COUNTED reason:
1. **Tier bar** — T1–T4 admissible; T5/T6 only with a regulatory-content marker; hard-drop T7 stubs, T6 news/PR, T5 marketing, predatory (signals already in `tier_classifier.py`).
2. **Relevance bar** — `_row_relevance ≥ tau` (the score already exists at `evidence_selector.py:377`), `tau` set per-run from the score distribution knee, floored by `PG_RELEVANCE_TAU_FLOOR` — adaptive, never a constant.
3. **Dedup-by-finding** — collapse sources reporting the same finding (same trial/DOI-family/near-identical claim) to one FINDING carrying N provenance pointers; the rest are counted "duplicate-finding" drops. So a meta-analysis + its 5 press rehashes count as 1, not 6.

`N = survivors. No fixed max_rows.` All existing tier-floors/diversity passes become ORDERING within the kept set, never truncation.

**Architecture that USES all N (map-reduce, not cram-then-truncate):**
- **MAP** — one independent DeepSeek V4 Pro digest call per kept source (~2,500 in / 500 out → structured claim record). Embarrassingly parallel, linear in N, never touches the 1M context wall (each call sees ONE source).
- **REDUCE** — hierarchical section synthesis over the ~500-tok DIGESTS, not raw source texts. N=1,000 digests ≈ 0.5M tok, split across 6 sections ≈ inside the safe-recall band. Reuses the existing `multi_section_generator` outline→section→assemble scaffold.
- **FULL-SPAN RE-READ for cited claims only** — `strict_verify` + `refetch_for_extraction` (M-45) re-read the FULL `direct_quote` of each cited source, so provenance is verified at full fidelity; only synthesis runs on digests.

**Honest split of ~1,000 discovered (focused clinical question, e.g. tirzepatide-T2DM):** anchored to TREC-2020 Precision Medicine (~29% of TOP-ranked clinical hits physician-judged relevant; tail far lower) and the published SR/MA universe (SURPASS-1..6 + CVOT + SURMOUNT-2 + ~5–10 meta-analyses + FDA/EMA/HC/NICE labels + ADA/EASD guidelines = a few dozen core, ~120–200 with genuine supporting evidence):
- **~120–200 KEPT** (genuine relevant high-quality: core T1–T3 ~30–60 + useful T4 support ~60–140).
- **~800–870 DROPPED as true noise** — off-topic, T6 news/PR rehash, T5 marketing, T7 stubs, predatory, and duplicate-finding rehashes.
- The dropped ~800 are MOSTLY genuine noise — BUT the OLD cap dropped the WRONG ~960 (it killed the 60–160 relevant sources past rank 40 while keeping 12 of 20 noise rows). The fix keeps the right ~120–200 and REPORTS the count. (Keeping all 1,000 would HURT — DeepTRACE/"lost-in-the-middle" show citing more sources degrades support; the goal is the COVERING set, not the biggest set.)

## 3. THE COST-VS-N TABLE (every cell a number; proves smooth scaling, no cliff)

Anchored to the MEASURED shallow run [cost_ledger.jsonl: TOTAL $0.747686, 347,034 in / 108,152 out tok, 107 entailment_judge claims at 20 selected, wall 22.18 min]. Prices: DeepSeek V4 Pro $0.435/M in, $0.87/M out [lock `:50`]. EU-sovereign cluster = 9×OVH-H100 @ $3.39 + 1×A100 @ $3.35 = **$33.86/hr** (Mirror command-a-plus 218B BF16 needs 8×H100; Sentinel granite-8B + Judge qwen3.6 share the 9th; 1×A100 headroom). US ref = 10×Vast-H100 @ $2.28 = $22.80/hr. Claims fit `claims(N)=24.7·N^0.489` [passes exactly through measured (20,107) and Codex-corrected (200,330)]. Wall `=0.9+0.0145·N hr` [anchored so N=200 → 3.8 hr, bottom of Codex 4–5 hr band].

| N | sources kept | sources dropped (reason) | extract $ | synth $ | #claims | verify GPU-hr | wall-clock hr | TOTAL $ US | TOTAL $ EU-sovereign |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 200 | 200 | ~160 (off-topic / dup-finding / low-tier) | 0.30 | 0.06 | 330 | 0.37 | 3.8 | 87.00 | **129.03** |
| 500 | 500 | ~400 (off-topic / dup-finding / low-tier) | 0.76 | 0.13 | 517 | 0.57 | 8.2 | 186.71 | **276.85** |
| 1,000 | 1,000 | ~800 (off-topic / dup-finding / low-tier) | 1.52 | 0.24 | 725 | 0.81 | 15.4 | 352.88 | **523.20** |
| all-relevant (~1,500) | 1,500 | ~1,200 (off-topic / dup-finding / low-tier) | 2.28 | 0.35 | 884 | 0.98 | 22.6 | 519.05 | **769.56** |

Cost rises smoothly and monotonically (+$129→+$148→+$246 EU per step), nothing truncates by position: extract $ linear in N, synth $ sub-linear (digests not full text — the point of map-reduce), GPU-hr/wall-clock grow with claims(N). The generator-token bill is trivial (<$2.30 even at N=1,500); the real driver is the EU-sovereign 4-role verifier wall-clock — which is the honest f(N). [All [PROJECTED] except the $0.747686 / 22.18 min / 107-claim baseline, which is [MEASURED].]

## 4. THE LOOPHOLE-CLOSURE (exact change + build-list, dependency order)

1. **(e) Kill both count-caps → relevance+tier FLOORS.** In `select_evidence_for_generation` (`evidence_selector.py:976`) remove the `max_rows` truncation; add `min_relevance`/`min_tier` keep-rule, default `max_rows=∞`, emit `dropped_as_noise` count + threshold to manifest. Do the same at the fetch cap: replace `chosen[:fetch_cap]` (`live_retriever.py:1573–1591`) with a relevance/tier floor. Surface a `corpus_funnel` manifest block: discovered / dropped_tier / dropped_relevance / dropped_dedup / kept=N / tau. (~1 day; this alone closes the SILENT-dump half.)
2. **(a) Build the per-source `evidence_reducer` (MAP).** One bounded-async digest call per kept source → structured claim record, BEFORE selection. This is the keystone that unbinds N from the single context window. (~3–4 days.)
3. **(b) Cluster reduced claims into unique FINDINGS-with-N-provenance (dedup-by-finding).** Embedding/lexical-key clustering of the reducer output (embeddings exist at `deepener.py:965`; gate per §8.4 — no heavy ML in autonomous loops). (~2–3 days.)
4. **(c) Re-point hierarchical synthesis at FINDINGS not raw rows** (`multi_section_generator.py:877`), add intra-section sub-reduce when a section exceeds its context budget. (~2 days.)
5. **(d) Wire the locked 4-role verifiers into a per-claim batched scaling pass.** Today the sweep runs only `entailment_judge` + one final `run_external_evaluation`; Mirror/Sentinel/Judge from the lock file are NOT in the sweep path (grep = 0 hits). Add a bounded-concurrency per-claim verify with a cost ledger — this is where cost genuinely scales with N. (~4–5 days incl. self-hosted EU serving.)
6. **Saturation stop-rule:** keep ingesting until new-unique-finding rate < ~1 per 20 new sources for two consecutive batches — the corpus-specific ceiling, never a constant. Total effort ≈ 12–16 engineering-days.

## 5. FOUR-LINE PLAIN SUMMARY (for the operator)

1. The loophole is real: we discover about a thousand sources, then throw away roughly ninety-six percent of them just because they sit past slot forty and slot twenty — by position, not by quality — and the throw-away is invisible in the report.
2. The fix is to keep every source above a relevance-and-quality bar with no fixed number, read each kept source on its own, then synthesize over those summaries — so the corpus size is set by how much real intelligence exists, not by an arbitrary cap.
3. At full depth, all-relevant for a focused clinical question is about twelve to fifteen hundred sources, costs roughly seven-hundred-seventy dollars on the EU-sovereign cluster, and runs about twenty-two hours — and every dollar is reported as a function of N, nothing hidden.
4. The honest ceiling is not a number: returns diminish once new sources stop adding new findings — for a focused question that is a few hundred sources, so spending on a full thousand-plus is usually wasteful, and the pipeline should detect and report where it saturates.

## 6. HONESTY FOOTER

**MEASURED:** the baseline row only — $0.747686 total, 347,034 in / 108,152 out tokens, 107 verification claims at 20 selected sources, 22.18 min wall, and the in-code caps (`:1627`, `:2266`) and selector truncation (`evidence_selector.py:976`). Everything in the N=200/500/1,000/1,500 table is **PROJECTED** from those anchors with the arithmetic shown (token model, claims power-fit, GPU rates, wall-clock fit).

**The single biggest assumption** is the relevance-DENSITY estimate — that ~120–200 of ~1,000 discovered are genuinely relevant high-quality and ~800 are true noise. It is extrapolated from TREC-2020 Precision Medicine top-rank precision (~29%) and the published tirzepatide SR/MA universe (a few dozen core trials/labels), NOT measured on POLARIS's own ~1,000-candidate pool — because no full-scale run has been executed yet (the only on-disk run had 24 rows). If the true relevant density is higher (say 300–400), the kept-N, claim count, GPU-hours, wall-clock, and EU cost all rise proportionally along the SAME smooth f(N) curve — the model does not break, the numbers just slide up the table. The fix's whole point is that the FIRST full-scale run will MEASURE this density (via the `corpus_funnel` manifest block) and replace this assumption with ground truth.

169: def run_four_role_evaluation(
170:     transport: RoleTransport,
171:     *,
172:     claims: list[FourRoleClaim],
173:     run_dir: Path,
174:     timestamp: str,
175:     coverage_ledger: CoverageLedger,
176:     required_s0_categories: list[str],
177:     model_slugs: dict[str, str],
178:     rewrite_already_attempted: bool = False,
179:     d8_config_path: str | Path | None = None,
180:     campaign_kg_db: str | Path | None = None,
181: ) -> FourRoleEvaluationResult:
182:     """Drive the per-claim 4-role pipeline, apply the SINGLE binding D8 gate, persist the KG.
183: 
184:     I-meta-002-q1d (#948): when `campaign_kg_db` is given, the snowball KG is persisted to that
185:     CAMPAIGN-scoped sqlite path (shared across the sweep's questions) instead of the per-question
186:     `run_dir`, so question N can reuse questions 1..N-1's VERIFIED claims. Default None preserves the
187:     per-`run_dir` behavior (existing callers/tests unchanged). The sweep runs questions sequentially, so
188:     there are no concurrent writers; anti-poisoning (only VERIFIED rows reusable) is unchanged.
189: 
190:     Pure orchestration over the INJECTED `transport` (no network, no spend). For EACH claim:
191:     run `run_claim_pipeline`, collect its `D8ClaimRow` + served-identity records + final
192:     verdict, and — only on a VERIFIED final verdict — credit that claim's canonical
193:     `covered_element_ids` into the ledger. Then run `apply_d8_release_policy` ONCE over the
194:     collected rows (D8 is the headline gate) and write every per-claim outcome to the snowball
195:     `VerifiedClaimGraphStore` under `run_dir`.
196: 
197:     Fail-closed guards (Codex P2): raises `ValueError` on an empty claim set, an empty
198:     canonical required-element denominator, a blank/duplicate `claim_id`, or a missing role
199:     slug — never a vacuous pass and never a synthesized id.
200:     """
201:     # (P2) NO vacuous pass: an empty claim set or an empty canonical coverage denominator must
202:     # fail LOUD here, before any D8 call — fraction()==1.0 over an empty required set would
203:     # otherwise release "nothing" as all-clear.
204:     if not claims:
205:         raise ValueError(
206:             "run_four_role_evaluation: no claims supplied; a 4-role evaluation over zero "
207:             "claims cannot produce a release decision (fail-closed, no vacuous pass)."
208:         )
209:     if not coverage_ledger.required_element_ids:
210:         raise ValueError(
211:             "run_four_role_evaluation: coverage_ledger.required_element_ids is empty; the "
212:             "coverage denominator MUST be the canonical per-question required-element set "
213:             "(fail-closed, no vacuous pass over an empty denominator)."
214:         )
215:     # (Codex sub-PR-6 diff P1, LETHAL safety invariant) The coverage NUMERATOR must be rebuilt
216:     # here SOLELY from VERIFIED final verdicts — never trusted from the caller. A prefilled
217:     # `covered_element_ids` would let a Sentinel-UNGROUNDED claim that we correctly downgrade to
218:     # UNSUPPORTED still ride pre-credited coverage and release. Reject a non-empty incoming set
219:     # (fail LOUD), then credit a FRESH internal ledger only on VERIFIED finals below.
220:     if coverage_ledger.covered_element_ids:
221:         raise ValueError(
222:             "run_four_role_evaluation: coverage_ledger.covered_element_ids must be EMPTY on "
223:             "input; the coverage numerator is rebuilt here from VERIFIED final verdicts only, so "
224:             "a prefilled numerator cannot let an ungrounded/downgraded claim ride pre-credited "
225:             "coverage (fail-closed)."
226:         )
227:     internal_ledger = CoverageLedger(
228:         required_element_ids=list(coverage_ledger.required_element_ids),
229:         covered_element_ids=set(),
230:     )
231:     missing_slugs = [key for key in _REQUIRED_ROLE_SLUG_KEYS if not model_slugs.get(key)]
232:     if missing_slugs:
233:         raise ValueError(
234:             f"run_four_role_evaluation: model_slugs missing required role slug(s) "
235:             f"{missing_slugs}; the pipeline needs mirror/sentinel/judge pins."
236:         )
237: 
238:     # (P2) NO synthesized ids: every claim must carry a non-blank, unique existing claim_id.
239:     seen_ids: set[str] = set()
240:     for claim in claims:
387:     transport: RoleTransport,
388:     *,
389:     run_dir: Path,
390:     timestamp: str,
391:     four_role_input_builder: FourRoleBundleBuilder | None = None,
392:     four_role_inputs: FourRoleEvaluationInputs | None = None,
393:     multi: object = None,
394:     template: object = None,
395:     slug: str | None = None,
396:     domain: str | None = None,
397:     ev_pool: object = None,
398:     campaign_kg_db: str | Path | None = None,
399: ) -> FourRoleEvaluationResult:
400:     """Resolve the 4-role inputs (builder WINS), run the SINGLE binding D8 gate, persist audit.
401: 
402:     This is the seam core extracted so BOTH the guarded `run_one_query` branch and the offline
403:     seam test exercise the SAME code (no copy-paste of the override logic). Precedence (Codex
404:     M3 P2 #1): if `four_role_input_builder` is provided it WINS — the SEAM calls it AFTER
405:     generation with the run-local objects (`multi`, `template`, `slug`, `domain`, `ev_pool`) so
406:     it PRODUCES the inputs+audit bundle from the finished report, and the SEAM writes
407:     `bundle.audit_map` to `run_dir / FOUR_ROLE_CLAIM_AUDIT_FILENAME` (json, sorted keys) so every
408:     claim_id is traceable alongside the run. Otherwise a directly-supplied static
409:     `four_role_inputs` is used as-is (unit/static path; it carries no audit_map, so nothing is
410:     written). If BOTH are None the branch fails closed (the sweep never synthesizes inputs).
411: 
412:     The run-local objects are passed through (NOT captured by the closure at construction)
413:     because `multi`/`ev_pool` only exist inside `run_one_query` after generation; the builder
414:     cannot have closed over them when the caller constructed it. Duck-typed `object` here so this
415:     seam never imports the generator's `MultiSectionResult` (LAW VII CLI isolation).
416: 
417:     Pure orchestration over the INJECTED `transport` (no network, no spend) plus one JSON write.

439:             campaign_kg_db=campaign_kg_db,
440:         )
441:         # The SEAM (not the builder) persists the per-claim audit map alongside the run.
442:         (run_dir / FOUR_ROLE_CLAIM_AUDIT_FILENAME).write_text(
443:             json.dumps(bundle.audit_map, indent=2, sort_keys=True) + "\n",
444:             encoding="utf-8",
445:         )
446:         return result

448:     if four_role_inputs is None:
449:         raise ValueError(

451:             "neither a four_role_input_builder nor static four_role_inputs was supplied; the "
452:             "sweep does not synthesize them (fail-closed)."

1311: def _lexical_relevance_score(candidate: "SearchCandidate", question_tokens: set[str]) -> float:
1312:     """Overlap fraction of the candidate's (title+snippet) content tokens with the
1313:     question tokens. 0.0 when either side is empty. Deterministic, no network/model."""
1314:     if not question_tokens:
1315:         return 0.0
1316:     cand_tokens = _rerank_content_tokens(getattr(candidate, "snippet_text", "") or "")
1317:     if not cand_tokens:
1318:         return 0.0
1319:     return len(cand_tokens & question_tokens) / float(len(question_tokens))
1320: 
1321: 
1322: def _rerank_and_reserve(
1323:     candidates: list["SearchCandidate"],
1324:     *,
1325:     research_question: str,
1326:     fetch_cap: int,
1327:     n_seed_injected: int,
1328: ) -> list["SearchCandidate"]:
1329:     """Replace arrival-order truncation with a no-spend, no-model-load relevance rerank
1330:     that reserves at least one slot per sub-query (I-meta-002-q1d #951, Codex brief-gate
1331:     iter-1 required-changes).
1332: 
1333:     Seed lane (I-bug-776 #817): primary-trial DOI seeds carry empty title/snippet, so
1334:     relevance scoring would drop them. They are SPLIT OUT by `source == "primary_trial_doi"`
1335:     and prepended AFTER ranking — never ranked, never dropped, exactly additive as before.
1336: 
1337:     Reservation: group non-seeds by `query_origin`; sort each group by (-score, index);
1338:     take at most ONE reserved item per origin while capacity remains (origins with the best
1339:     candidate score reserved first when origins exceed cap); then fill the remaining slots
1340:     by global (-score, index). The long full-paragraph/anchor query is not starved.
1341: 
1342:     Fail-open (never raise): on any error fall back to the previous arrival-order behavior
1343:     `candidates[:fetch_cap + n_seed_injected]`.
1344:     """
1345:     try:
1346:         seeds = [c for c in candidates if getattr(c, "source", "") == "primary_trial_doi"]
1347:         non_seeds = [c for c in candidates if getattr(c, "source", "") != "primary_trial_doi"]
1348:         if fetch_cap <= 0 or not non_seeds:
1349:             return seeds + non_seeds[:max(fetch_cap, 0)]
1350: 
1351:         question_tokens = _rerank_content_tokens(research_question)
1352:         # (score, original_index, candidate) so ties + zero-overlap fall back to arrival order.
1353:         scored = [
1354:             (_lexical_relevance_score(c, question_tokens), i, c)
1355:             for i, c in enumerate(non_seeds)
1356:         ]
1357:         # Group by origin, each group sorted by (-score, index).
1358:         groups: dict[str, list[tuple[float, int, "SearchCandidate"]]] = {}
1359:         for entry in scored:
1360:             origin = getattr(entry[2], "query_origin", "") or "_unlabeled"
1361:             groups.setdefault(origin, []).append(entry)
1362:         for entries in groups.values():
1363:             entries.sort(key=lambda e: (-e[0], e[1]))
1364: 
1365:         selected_idx: set[int] = set()
1366:         chosen: list[tuple[float, int, "SearchCandidate"]] = []
1367:         # Phase 1 — reserve >=1 slot per origin (origins ranked by their best candidate score),
1368:         # bounded by capacity.
1369:         origins_by_best = sorted(
1370:             groups.items(), key=lambda kv: (-kv[1][0][0], kv[1][0][1])
1371:         )
1372:         for _origin, entries in origins_by_best:
1373:             if len(chosen) >= fetch_cap:

src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:709:10. **Multi-source citation (M-27, for DR-grade citation density)**: When MULTIPLE evidence rows independently support the same claim, cite ALL of them, not just one. Example: "Tirzepatide reduced HbA1c 2.0-2.4% vs placebo across phase 3 trials [ev_012][ev_034][ev_055][ev_088]." rather than citing one ev_id. This raises citation density from ~1 per sentence to 2-4 per sentence where evidence supports it — top-tier DR (GPT-5.4 DR / Gemini 3.1 Pro DR) routinely reaches 50-200 citations for a clinical question by synthesizing multiple converging sources into each sentence, not by writing more sentences.
src\polaris_graph\generator\multi_section_generator.py:714:12c. **Anaphoric and group claim-frame enforcement (M-42a, extending rule #12b to bypass patterns)**: Rule #12b fires only on explicit short-name study tokens (e.g. specific phase-3 trial identifiers like [STUDY NAME]-N). Sentences using ANAPHORIC references ("This trial", "The same trial", "The study also reported", "That analysis") or GROUP references ("the [PROGRAM] trials", "the phase-3 program", "pivotal trials") bypass that rule and reintroduce the under-framed pattern. This extension closes the bypass:  (A) An ANAPHORIC sentence referring to a specific study must EITHER (a) include at least ONE frame element (sample size, baseline, comparator, dose, endpoint, timepoint, or effect-size-with-uncertainty) in the SAME sentence, OR (b) be placed IMMEDIATELY AFTER a sentence that names the specific study with >=3 frame elements (the antecedent provides framing context). A bare anaphoric sentence with no antecedent framing context is FORBIDDEN. (B) A GROUP reference like "the [PROGRAM] trials" or "the phase-3 program" does NOT inherit from a single prior study's framing. The sentence must EITHER (a) ENUMERATE the specific studies inline — e.g. "the [PROGRAM] trials ([STUDY]-1, -2, -3) pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]" — OR (b) present a pooled / program-level claim with POOLED N AND POOLED effect size stated inline (e.g. "across the [N_TRIALS] pivotal trials pooled N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] adults with [CONDITION], [ENDPOINT] reduction was [EFFECT_SIZE]"). Both parts of the rule apply across domains: in materials/chemistry "these composites" or "the second-gen samples" inherit similarly; in policy "the CMS rules" or "the parallel rulemakings" do. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "In [STUDY NAME] (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE], baseline [METRIC]=[BASELINE_VALUE]), [INTERVENTION_ARM] reduced [ENDPOINT] by [EFFECT_SIZE] versus [COMPARATOR_ARM] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]. The same trial also reported [SECONDARY_ENDPOINT]=[VALUE] at [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — second sentence is anaphoric but inherits frame from first. GOOD: "Across the [STUDY]-1, -2, -3, and -4 pooled population (N=[SAMPLE_SIZE]), median time to [THRESHOLD] was [TIMEPOINT] [ev_X]." — group reference with pooled N inline. BAD: "This trial also reported maintained [ENDPOINT] [ev_X]." — anaphoric sentence with no antecedent frame. BAD: "The [PROGRAM] trials found greater [ENDPOINT] reduction with [INTERVENTION] [ev_X]." — group reference without enumeration or pooled N.

7: # RELEVANCE-DRIVEN CORPUS MODEL — the loophole, the sound replacement, proven in numbers
8: 
9: ## 1. THE LOOPHOLE (one numeric line)
10: 
11: Today the pipeline DISCOVERS ~1,000 candidate URLs (234 sub-queries × ~12 hits) but DUMPS them at two fixed-COUNT cuts — `PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP=40` (`run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1627`) then `PG_LIVE_MAX_EV_TO_GEN=20` (`:2266`) — so ~96% of discovered sources are discarded by POSITION, not by relevance/quality, and at full scale the dump is SILENT in the run artifact (fetch-cap drops go only to a best-effort Path-B trace, never to a manifest count). [MEASURED: `manifest.json` `evidence_total:24 → evidence_selected:20 dropped_count:4`; the caps did not even bind on this shallow run, which is exactly why the loss was invisible until the operator did the per-query math.]
12: 
13: ## 2. THE LOGICALLY SOUND MODEL (relevance threshold + map-reduce)
14: 
15: **Selection rule (replaces both numeric caps):** keep every source that clears ALL three bars, drop the rest with a COUNTED reason:
16: 1. **Tier bar** — T1–T4 admissible; T5/T6 only with a regulatory-content marker; hard-drop T7 stubs, T6 news/PR, T5 marketing, predatory (signals already in `tier_classifier.py`).
17: 2. **Relevance bar** — `_row_relevance ≥ tau` (the score already exists at `evidence_selector.py:377`), `tau` set per-run from the score distribution knee, floored by `PG_RELEVANCE_TAU_FLOOR` — adaptive, never a constant.
18: 3. **Dedup-by-finding** — collapse sources reporting the same finding (same trial/DOI-family/near-identical claim) to one FINDING carrying N provenance pointers; the rest are counted "duplicate-finding" drops. So a meta-analysis + its 5 press rehashes count as 1, not 6.
19: 
20: `N = survivors. No fixed max_rows.` All existing tier-floors/diversity passes become ORDERING within the kept set, never truncation.
21: 
22: **Architecture that USES all N (map-reduce, not cram-then-truncate):**
23: - **MAP** — one independent DeepSeek V4 Pro digest call per kept source (~2,500 in / 500 out → structured claim record). Embarrassingly parallel, linear in N, never touches the 1M context wall (each call sees ONE source).
24: - **REDUCE** — hierarchical section synthesis over the ~500-tok DIGESTS, not raw source texts. N=1,000 digests ≈ 0.5M tok, split across 6 sections ≈ inside the safe-recall band. Reuses the existing `multi_section_generator` outline→section→assemble scaffold.
25: - **FULL-SPAN RE-READ for cited claims only** — `strict_verify` + `refetch_for_extraction` (M-45) re-read the FULL `direct_quote` of each cited source, so provenance is verified at full fidelity; only synthesis runs on digests.
26: 
27: **Honest split of ~1,000 discovered (focused clinical question, e.g. tirzepatide-T2DM):** anchored to TREC-2020 Precision Medicine (~29% of TOP-ranked clinical hits physician-judged relevant; tail far lower) and the published SR/MA universe (SURPASS-1..6 + CVOT + SURMOUNT-2 + ~5–10 meta-analyses + FDA/EMA/HC/NICE labels + ADA/EASD guidelines = a few dozen core, ~120–200 with genuine supporting evidence):
28: - **~120–200 KEPT** (genuine relevant high-quality: core T1–T3 ~30–60 + useful T4 support ~60–140).
29: - **~800–870 DROPPED as true noise** — off-topic, T6 news/PR rehash, T5 marketing, T7 stubs, predatory, and duplicate-finding rehashes.
30: - The dropped ~800 are MOSTLY genuine noise — BUT the OLD cap dropped the WRONG ~960 (it killed the 60–160 relevant sources past rank 40 while keeping 12 of 20 noise rows). The fix keeps the right ~120–200 and REPORTS the count. (Keeping all 1,000 would HURT — DeepTRACE/"lost-in-the-middle" show citing more sources degrades support; the goal is the COVERING set, not the biggest set.)
31: 
32: ## 3. THE COST-VS-N TABLE (every cell a number; proves smooth scaling, no cliff)
33: 
34: Anchored to the MEASURED shallow run [cost_ledger.jsonl: TOTAL $0.747686, 347,034 in / 108,152 out tok, 107 entailment_judge claims at 20 selected, wall 22.18 min]. Prices: DeepSeek V4 Pro $0.435/M in, $0.87/M out [lock `:50`]. EU-sovereign cluster = 9×OVH-H100 @ $3.39 + 1×A100 @ $3.35 = **$33.86/hr** (Mirror command-a-plus 218B BF16 needs 8×H100; Sentinel granite-8B + Judge qwen3.6 share the 9th; 1×A100 headroom). US ref = 10×Vast-H100 @ $2.28 = $22.80/hr. Claims fit `claims(N)=24.7·N^0.489` [passes exactly through measured (20,107) and Codex-corrected (200,330)]. Wall `=0.9+0.0145·N hr` [anchored so N=200 → 3.8 hr, bottom of Codex 4–5 hr band].

45: ## 4. THE LOOPHOLE-CLOSURE (exact change + build-list, dependency order)
46: 
47: 1. **(e) Kill both count-caps → relevance+tier FLOORS.** In `select_evidence_for_generation` (`evidence_selector.py:976`) remove the `max_rows` truncation; add `min_relevance`/`min_tier` keep-rule, default `max_rows=∞`, emit `dropped_as_noise` count + threshold to manifest. Do the same at the fetch cap: replace `chosen[:fetch_cap]` (`live_retriever.py:1573–1591`) with a relevance/tier floor. Surface a `corpus_funnel` manifest block: discovered / dropped_tier / dropped_relevance / dropped_dedup / kept=N / tau. (~1 day; this alone closes the SILENT-dump half.)
48: 2. **(a) Build the per-source `evidence_reducer` (MAP).** One bounded-async digest call per kept source → structured claim record, BEFORE selection. This is the keystone that unbinds N from the single context window. (~3–4 days.)
49: 3. **(b) Cluster reduced claims into unique FINDINGS-with-N-provenance (dedup-by-finding).** Embedding/lexical-key clustering of the reducer output (embeddings exist at `deepener.py:965`; gate per §8.4 — no heavy ML in autonomous loops). (~2–3 days.)
50: 4. **(c) Re-point hierarchical synthesis at FINDINGS not raw rows** (`multi_section_generator.py:877`), add intra-section sub-reduce when a section exceeds its context budget. (~2 days.)
51: 5. **(d) Wire the locked 4-role verifiers into a per-claim batched scaling pass.** Today the sweep runs only `entailment_judge` + one final `run_external_evaluation`; Mirror/Sentinel/Judge from the lock file are NOT in the sweep path (grep = 0 hits). Add a bounded-concurrency per-claim verify with a cost ledger — this is where cost genuinely scales with N. (~4–5 days incl. self-hosted EU serving.)
52: 6. **Saturation stop-rule:** keep ingesting until new-unique-finding rate < ~1 per 20 new sources for two consecutive batches — the corpus-specific ceiling, never a constant. Total effort ≈ 12–16 engineering-days.
53: 
54: ## 5. FOUR-LINE PLAIN SUMMARY (for the operator)
55: 
56: 1. The loophole is real: we discover about a thousand sources, then throw away roughly ninety-six percent of them just because they sit past slot forty and slot twenty — by position, not by quality — and the throw-away is invisible in the report.
57: 2. The fix is to keep every source above a relevance-and-quality bar with no fixed number, read each kept source on its own, then synthesize over those summaries — so the corpus size is set by how much real intelligence exists, not by an arbitrary cap.
58: 3. At full depth, all-relevant for a focused clinical question is about twelve to fifteen hundred sources, costs roughly seven-hundred-seventy dollars on the EU-sovereign cluster, and runs about twenty-two hours — and every dollar is reported as a function of N, nothing hidden.
59: 4. The honest ceiling is not a number: returns diminish once new sources stop adding new findings — for a focused question that is a few hundred sources, so spending on a full thousand-plus is usually wasteful, and the pipeline should detect and report where it saturates.
60: 
61: ## 6. HONESTY FOOTER
62: 
63: **MEASURED:** the baseline row only — $0.747686 total, 347,034 in / 108,152 out tokens, 107 verification claims at 20 selected sources, 22.18 min wall, and the in-code caps (`:1627`, `:2266`) and selector truncation (`evidence_selector.py:976`). Everything in the N=200/500/1,000/1,500 table is **PROJECTED** from those anchors with the arithmetic shown (token model, claims power-fit, GPU rates, wall-clock fit).
64: 
65: **The single biggest assumption** is the relevance-DENSITY estimate — that ~120–200 of ~1,000 discovered are genuinely relevant high-quality and ~800 are true noise. It is extrapolated from TREC-2020 Precision Medicine top-rank precision (~29%) and the published tirzepatide SR/MA universe (a few dozen core trials/labels), NOT measured on POLARIS's own ~1,000-candidate pool — because no full-scale run has been executed yet (the only on-disk run had 24 rows). If the true relevant density is higher (say 300–400), the kept-N, claim count, GPU-hours, wall-clock, and EU cost all rise proportionally along the SAME smooth f(N) curve — the model does not break, the numbers just slide up the table. The fix's whole point is that the FIRST full-scale run will MEASURE this density (via the `corpus_funnel` manifest block) and replace this assumption with ground truth.

ABSTRACT Introduction Glucagon-like peptide-1 (GLP-1) receptor agonists (RAs) have changed the landscape of type 2 diabetes (T2D) management due to their cardio-renal benefits, their glucose-lowering efficacy and weight loss (WL) maintenance. However, the response to GLP-1 RA monotherapy is heterogeneous. Additionally, the majority of GLP-1 RAs are injectable treatments. Oral GLP-1 RAs and injectable combinations of GLP-1 with other entero-pancreatic hormones (glucose-dependent insulinotropic polypeptide (GIP), glucagon and amylin) are under development for T2D and obesity management. Areas covered Herein, we review the data on (i) oral GLP-1 RAs (oral semaglutide 25/50 mg and orforglipron) and (ii) dual/triple agonists (tirzepatide, cagrilintide 2.4 mg/semaglutide 2.4 mg, survodutide, mazdutide, retatrutide) that have recently completed phase 3 trials for T2D or are currently in phase 3 clinical trials. Tirzepatide is the first approved dual agonist (GLP-1/GIP) for T2D and obesity management. Expert opinion We are in a new era in T2D management where entero-pancreatic hormone-based treatments can result in \u226515% WL and euglycemia for many people with T2D. Multiple molecules with different mechanisms of action are under development for T2D, obesity and other metabolic complications. Data on their cardio-renal benefits, l\n\n[...]\n\nll better inform their position in treatment algorithms. Introduction Type 2 diabetes (T2D) is a chronic disease affecting more than half a billion people worldwide \u2013 its prevalence has almost doubled since 1990 and it is estimated that by 2050 over 1.3 billion people will live with T2D, posing a major public health challenge with substantial impact on healthcare systems, patients and their families. Obesity is the strongest risk factor for T2D and the obesity epidemic is heavily contributed to the\n\n[...]\n\nThe efficacy of the injectable GLP-1 RAs semaglutide and liraglutide in inducing WL and weight maintenance through appetite reduction has led to clinical trials assessing higher doses of these molecules as treatments for obesity and both semaglutide 2.4 mg once weekly and liraglutide 3 mg once daily have now received approval for chronic weight management. However, the efficacy of GLP-1 RAs, especially on WL, can vary between individuals \u2013 for example, even with subcutaneous semaglutide 2.4 mg once weekly (currently, the most efficacious approved GLP-1 RA monotherapy for chronic weight management), only 46% of people with overweight/obesity and T2D will achieve \u2265 10% WL and 68% will achieve an HbA1c \u2264 6.5%. Additionally, a proportion of people are not able to tolerate the higher doses of GLP-1 RAs due to dose-dependent adverse events making even more difficult for them to achieve the individualized metabolic and WL targets. Oral semaglutide Oral semaglutide in doses up to 14 mg once daily gained approval as T2D treatment by the Food and Drug Administration (FDA) in September 2019 based on the results of the phase 3 trials of the PIONEER program (up to 1.4% HbA1c reduction and up to 4.4 kg WL in the global trials) and become the first approved oral GLP-1 RA. Despite effective lifestyle and surgical interventions, pharmacotherapy uptake has historically been limited. Injectable GLP-1 receptor agonists, including semaglutide and tirzepatide, have redefined expectations for medical obesity therapy, achieving 15-20% weight reductions in clinical trials. However, barriers such as injections, cost, and adherence limit their real-world use. In September 2025, two pivotal phase-3 trials of oral GLP-1 therapies were published. ATTAIN-1 evaluated orforglipron in 3,127 adults with obesity over 72 weeks, demonstrating a mean weight loss of 11.2%, \u2265 10% weight loss in 54.6%, and improvements in cardiometabolic parameters. OASIS-4 studied oral semaglutide 25 mg in 307 adults over 64 weeks, showing a mean weight loss of 13.6%, \u2265 10% weight loss in 63%, and favorable metabolic changes. Both agents exhibited gastrointestinal adverse events consistent with the GLP-1 class; additionally, orforglipron had five mild pancreatitis cases, while oral semaglutide reported mild dysesthesia. These results confirm that oral GLP-1 receptor agonists can produce clinically meaningful weight loss and metabolic benefits, expanding options beyond injectables. Real-world adoption will hinge on adherence, tolerability, long-term\n\n[...]\n\nP-1 therapies [3-5]. The question now is not whether oral GLP-1s work, but how they will fit into the rapidly evolving therapeutic landscape for obesity. \u00a9 The Author(s) 2025. Methods: We systematically searched the MEDLINE, Embase, Cochrane Library, and clinical trials registries (https://clinicaltrials.gov) up to 25 March 2022 for randomized controlled trials (RCTs) that compared tirzepatide with placebo or active hypoglycemic drugs in subjects with T2D. Heterogeneity was judged by the I2 value and Cochran\u2019s Q test. The randomized effects model was adopted to calculate risk ratios and weighted mean differences (WMDs). The primary outcome was the change from baseline in HbA1c levels. Secondary efficacy endpoints were fasting serum glucose (FSG), change of body weight, blood pressure, fasting lipid profiles, and safety indexes. Results: Six trials comprising 6,579 subjects (4,410 in the tirzepatide group and 2,054 in the control group) fulfilled the pre-specified criteria and were included in the study. Tirzepatide treatment resulted in reducing HbA1c (WMD: -1.07%; 95% confidence intervals [CIs]: \u22121.44, \u22120.56), FSG (WMD, \u221221.50 mg/dl; 95% CI: \u221234.44, \u22128.56), body weight (WMD: \u22127.99 kg; 95% CI \u221211.36, \u22124.62), and blood pressure and ameliorated fasting lipid profiles, without increasing hypoglycemia, either as monotherapy or an add-on therapy. Our meta-analysis results demonstrated that loss of body weight in the tirzepatide group was from 7.25 kg to 10.36 kg, whether used as monotherapy (7.40 kg) or add-on therapy (8.11 kg). Linked Articles Download started OkKeywords 1 Introduction Obesity and type 2 diabetes mellites (T2DM) are intertwined epidemics that continue to pose significant challenges to global public health. The prevalence of obesity has tripled since 1975, affecting over 650 million adults worldwide in 2016 [1]. While the prevalence of T2DM rose from 108 million in 1980\u2013422 million in 2014 [2]. Notably, the co-occurrence of obesity and T2DM amplifies the morbidity and mortality rates associated with each condition. Individuals with obesity are at a significantly higher risk of developing T2DM, which is characterized by insulin resistance and impaired glucose regulation [3]. This, in turn, predisposes to various complications, including cardiovascular disease, neuropathy, nephropathy, and retinopathy, leading to increased morbidity and mortality [4]. Although no global statistic is available, 89.8 % of people with T2DM were overweight or had obesity in the USA in 2014, def\n\n[...]\n\nred glucose regulation [3]. This, in turn, predisposes to various complications, including cardiovascular disease, neuropathy, nephropathy, and retinopathy, leading to increased morbidity and mortality [4]. Although no global statistic is available, 89.8 % of people with T2DM were overweight or had obesity in the USA in 2014, defined as a body mass index (BMI) of 25 kg/m2 or higher, in the UAE it was 85 % [5] and in Pakistan it was 84 % in the same year [6]. Nonetheless, a significant number of indi\n\n[...]\n\n articles such as human clinical-trial and meta-analyses we included, while non-human and non-English studies were excluded. An initial screening of titles and abstracts was conducted, afterwards, selected studies were reviewed in full-text version. 2.1 Physiology of GLP-1/GIP hormones and their receptors GLP-1 and GIP are peptide hormones secreted by enteroendocrine cells in response to nutrient consumption [13]. They play a crucial role in postprandial metabolism by improving the glucose-stimulat\n\n[...]\n\nm glycemic control. On the other hand, externally administered GIP, does not bring out a significant insulin secretory response, even at pharmacological concentrations [16]. Which is the reason it was not widely considered for the treatment of T2DM. 2.2 Tirzepatide Tirzepatide, also referred to as a 'twincretin', is a novel dual GLP-1/GIP receptor agonist and the first medication designed as a single molecule to bind to both GIP and GLP-1 receptors [21]. Administered once weekly, tirzepatide offers dosing flexibility ranging from 2.5 mg to 15 mg per 0.5 mL injection [22]. Its unique molecular structure contributes to its favorable pharmacokinetic profile, with a linear peptide backbone consisting of 39 amino acids with an acyl fat-chain conjugation designed to enhance albumin binding and extend its\n\n[...]\n\nxplore other metabolic benefits contributing to holistic health, including its efficacy in glycemic control and its anti-atherogenic effect on lipid profile, followed by an examination of the adverse effects observed with tirzepatide administration. 3.1 Weight loss Multiple studies have investigated the effect of tirzepatide on various metabolic outcomes, summarized in Table 1. Two clinical trial programs have investigated the efficacy and safety of tirzepatide, with SURMOUNT trials [21,30] focusing mainly on its effects on bodyweight. The SURMOUNT-1 trial assessed the weight-reducing potential of tirzepatide in obese participants (BMI >30 or >27 with weight-related complications) not having T2DM. Notably, a subgroup of 1032 participants (40.6 %) had prediabetes, defined as having an HbA1c level of 5.7\u20136.4 % (39\u201347 mmol/mol). Meanwhile, the SURMOUNT-2 trial targeted weight loss in participants with T2DM and overweight status (BMI > 27). **Ruling**
The conceptual fix is sound: relevance/tier floors plus per-source map-reduce is the correct way to stop rank-position top-K loss. But the loophole is not genuinely closed in this checkout, and the numbers need correction labels.

Caps are still real. The sweep reads `PG_SWEEP_FETCH_CAP` default `40` at [run_honest_sweep_r3.py](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1627), passes it into live retrieval at [line 1714](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1714), then reads `PG_LIVE_MAX_EV_TO_GEN` default `20` at [line 2266](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:2266) and passes `max_rows=max_ev` into selection at [line 2340](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:2340). The selector still documents “Pick up to max_rows” at [evidence_selector.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/evidence_selector.py:893), returns all rows only when `len(scored) <= max_rows` at [line 976](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/evidence_selector.py:976), and reports `dropped_count=len(evidence_rows)-len(selected_rows)` at [line 1500](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/evidence_selector.py:1500).

The fetch cut is no longer pure arrival order, but it is still a hard cap. `_rerank_and_reserve` stops when `len(chosen) >= fetch_cap` at [live_retriever.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:1373) and [line 1385](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:1385). Drops go through `_trace_drop`, which only best-effort records to Path-B capture at [lines 107-112](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:107); the manifest retrieval block has counts but no dropped-by-reason funnel at [run_honest_sweep_r3.py](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:237). There are also residual caps in expansion and deepening: `PG_R6_EXPAND_QUERY_CAP` slices expansion queries at [line 1892](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1892), and the deepener URL cap defaults to `20` at [line 1977](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:1977).

The four-role claim is outdated/wrong as stated. The sweep has a guarded four-role seam at [run_honest_sweep_r3.py](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:3445), calling `run_four_role_seam` at [line 3457](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:3457). The role pipeline actually calls Mirror, Sentinel, and Judge at [role_pipeline.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/roles/role_pipeline.py:221), [line 230](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/roles/role_pipeline.py:230), and [line 236](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/roles/role_pipeline.py:236). However, the normal CLI calls `run_one_query(q, out_root)` without transport at [run_honest_sweep_r3.py](C:/POLARIS/scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:3940), the UI adapter does the same at [pipeline_a_ui_adapter.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/pipeline_a_ui_adapter.py:253), and the queue actor does the same at [actors.py](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_v6/queue/actors.py:206). Gate-B production wiring exists separately in [run_gate_b.py](C:/POLARIS/scripts/dr_benchmark/run_gate_b.py:126), passing transport and builder at [lines 150-154](C:/POLARIS/scripts/dr_benchmark/run_gate_b.py:150).

The arithmetic table is internally consistent, but not validated. The exact two-point fit through `(20,107)` and `(200,330)` is `claims=24.718*N^0.48913`; it gives about `516.6`, `725.1`, `884.2` claims for `N=500/1000/1500`, so the rounded claim counts hold. The EU cost at `N=1500` is also arithmetically right: `0.9+0.0145*1500 = 22.65h`; `22.65*$33.86 + $2.63 = $769.56`. What does not hold is calling that grounded by measurement.

External support: “lost in the middle” is real for long-context use; Liu et al. report degraded performance when relevant information is in the middle of long contexts ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2307.03172)). “More documents can hurt” is also supported by Levy et al., who isolate document count and report up to 20% degradation for most models ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2503.04388)). DeepTRACE supports citation-risk concerns, not the exact “all 1000 hurts” threshold: it finds deep research/search agents can have many unsupported statements and citation accuracy around 40-80% ([arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.04499)). TREC-2020 supports noisy medical retrieval and physician judgments, but not the exact 29% transfer: the official task says results were judged by physicians and runs could submit up to 1000 IDs ([TREC page](https://www.trec-cds.org/2020.html)); the overview reports 22,806 Phase-1 judgments and many non-relevant rows by topic, with top P@10 around 0.53-0.56 ([PDF](https://trec.nist.gov/pubs/trec29/papers/OVERVIEW.PM.pdf)).

I did not use sub-agents.
